# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Leader Election Patterns Across K8s Ecosystem

## Your Task

Compare leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that implement leader election: the lease-based election in k8s, the Raft-based leader in etcd, and how each handles leader failover and re-election.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

63-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of leader election implementations across Kubernetes and etcd. Let me create a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings comparing leader election in both systems:

### Kubernetes (Lease-Based Election)
- **Core Files**: `leaderelection.go`, `leasecandidate.go`, `resourcelock/` interface and implementations
- **Mechanism**: Distributed lease stored in Kubernetes API (Coordination/Lease objects)
- **Key Components**: 
  - `LeaderElector` class with configurable timings (LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod)
  - Atomic `Get/Update/Create` operations via Kubernetes API
  - `tryAcquireOrRenew()` with fast-path optimization for existing leaders
  - `renew()` loop continuously renews lease within RenewDeadline
- **Failover**: Automatic when leader fails to renew before RenewDeadline expires (~10 seconds default)

### etcd (Raft-Based Election)
- **Core Files**: `raft.go`, `server.go`, `embed/config.go`, Raft message transport, election APIs
- **Mechanism**: Raft consensus protocol embedded in the server
- **Key Components**:
  - `raftNode` with `tick()` for election timeout management
  - Election parameters: `ElectionTicks` (default 10), `TickMs` heartbeat interval
  - `updateLeadership()` callback on leader transitions
  - `Leader()` and `waitLeader()` for querying/waiting on leader
  - Pre-vote feature to reduce disruptive elections
- **Failover**: Automatic when heartbeat misses exceed ElectionTimeout (~1 second default)

### Key Differences
- **Speed**: etcd re-elects ~10x faster due to ticks vs clock-dependent timeouts
- **Quorum**: etcd requires majority; Kubernetes requires only API availability
- **Coordination**: Kubernetes uses atomic updates; etcd uses Ra
... (truncated)

The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. \\t}\\n92: \\tif lec.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading == nil {\\n93: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"OnStartedLeading callback must not be nil\\\")\\n94: \\t}\\n95: \\tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\\n96: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\\\")\\n97: \\t}\\n98: \\n99: \\tif lec.Lock == nil {\\n100: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"Lock must not be nil.\\\")\\n101: \\t}\\n102: \\tid := lec.Lock.Identity()\\n103: \\tif id == \\\"\\\" {\\n104: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"Lock identity is empty\\\")\\n105: \\t}\\n106: \\n107: \\tle := LeaderElector{\\n108: \\t\\tconfig:  lec,\\n109: \\t\\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\\n110: \\t\\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\\n111: \\t}\\n112: \\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\\n113: \\treturn &le, nil\\n114: }\\n115: \\n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\\n117: \\t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\\n118: \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\\n155: \\t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\\n156: \\t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\\n157: \\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\\n158: \\tReleaseOnCancel bool\\n159: \\n160: \\t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\\n161: \\tName string\\n162: \\n163: \\t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\\n164: \\t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\\n165: \\tCoordinated bool\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\\n170: //\\n171: // possible future callbacks:\\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\\n174: \\t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\\n175: \\tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\\n176: \\t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\\n177: \\t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\\n178: \\t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\\n179: \\t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\\n180: \\tOnStoppedLeading func()\\n181: \\t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\\n182: \\t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\\n183: \\t// leader when the client starts.\\n184: \\tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\\n185: }\\n186: \\n187: // LeaderElector is a leader election client.\\n188: type LeaderElector struct {\\n189: \\tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\\n190: \\t// internal bookkeeping\\n191: \\tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\\n192: \\tobservedRawRecord []byte\\n193: \\tobservedTime      time.Time\\n194: \\t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\\n195: \\t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\\n196: \\t// not yet been reported.\\n197: \\treportedLeader string\\n198: \\n199: \\t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\\n200: \\tclock clock.Clock\\n201: \\n202: \\t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\\n203: \\tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\\n204: \\n205: \\tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\\n206: }\\n207: \\n208: // Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\\n209: // before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\\n210: // stopped holding the leader lease\\n211: func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\\n212: \\tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\\n213: \\tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\\n214: \\n215: \\tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\\n216: \\t\\treturn // ctx signalled done\\n217: \\t}\\n218: \\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\\n219: \\tdefer cancel()\\n220: \\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\\n221: \\tle.renew(ctx)\\n222: }\\n223: \\n224: // RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\\n225: // fails to validate. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\\n241: func (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\\n242: \\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\\n243: }\\n244: \\n245: // IsLeader returns true if the last observed leader was this client else returns false.\\n246: func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\\n247: \\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\\n248: }\\n249: \\n250: // acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\\n251: // Returns false if ctx signals done.\\n252: func (le *LeaderElector)     "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n21: //\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n29: //\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n37: //\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n41: // availability.\n42: //\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n48: // to master availability.\n49: //\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. duration that non-leader candidates will\n121: \t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n122: \t// last observed ack.\n123: \t//\n124: \t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n125: \t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n126: \t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n127: \t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n128: \t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n129: \t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n130: \t// long waits in the scenario.\n131: \t//\n132: \t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n133: \tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n134: \t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n135: \t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n136: \t//\n137: \t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n138: \tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n139: \t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n140: \t// between tries of actions.\n141: \t//\n142: \t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n143: \tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n144: \n145: \t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n146: \t// events of the LeaderElector\n147: \tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n148: \n149: \t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n150: \t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n151: \tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n152: \n153: \t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n154: \t// when the run context is cancelled. through a **distributed lease mechanism** stored in Kubernetes API resources. The core implementation resides in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`:\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **LeaderElector** (leaderelection.go): The main client-side leader election manager that implements a time-based lease renewal pattern. The `LeaderElector` type manages the election lifecycle with configurable timing parameters:\\n   - `LeaseDuration`: How long the lease is held (default 15 seconds)\\n   - `RenewDeadline`: Time limit for renewing the lease (default 10 seconds)\\n   - `RetryPeriod`: Time between retry attempts (default 2 seconds)\\n\\n2. **Election Flow** (leaderelection.go: Run, acquire, renew, tryAcquireOrRenew):\\n   - `Run()` is the main entry point that orchestrates the election\\n   - `acquire()` loops attempting to acquire the initial leader lease\\n   - `tryAcquireOrRenew()` uses a fast-path optimization: existing leaders attempt optimistic updates before falling back to slow-path (full Get/Update cycle)\\n   - `renew()` continuously renews the lease via `PollUntilContextTimeout()` within the RenewDeadline window\\n   - Failover is automatic: when the leader fails to renew before `RenewDeadline` expires, other candidates acquire the lease\\n\\n3. **Resource Lock Interface** (resourcelock/interface.go): Abstracts the storage backend for leader records:\\n   - `Interface` type defines Get, Create, Update operations\\n   - Supports multiple backends: Leases (current standard), ConfigMaps, Endpoints (deprecated)\\n   - `LeaderElectionRecord` contains HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n\\n4. **LeaseLock Implementation** (resourcelock/leaselock.go): Uses Kubernetes Lease objects as the distributed lock:\\n   - Stores election metadata in `coordination.k8s.io/v1 Lease.Spec` fields\\n   - `Get()` retrieves the current lease and converts it to a LeaderElectionRecord\\n   - `Update()` atomically updates the lease with new holder identity and timestamps\\n   - Race-free via Kubernetes API's optimistic locking (ResourceVersion)\\n\\n5. **Coordinated Leader Election** (leasecandidate.go): ALPHA feature for graceful leader transitions:\\n   - `LeaseCandidate` objects allow multiple candidates to express preferences\\n   - Watches for `PingTime` field to know when leadership transitions are expected\\n   - Enables coordinated handoff rather than timeout-based failover\\n\\n**Failover & Re-election Mechanism:**\\n- No explicit heartbeat protocol; the lease serves as implicit proof of life\\n- Re-election is triggered when:\\n  - Current leader fails to renew within `RenewDeadline` (typically 10 seconds)\\n  - Other candidates detect stale `RenewTime` timestamp\\n  - New leader elected by atomic Lease update (Kubernetes API handles conflict resolution)\\n- Clock skew tolerance: Configurable via RenewDeadline/LeaseDuration ratio (documented in leaderelection.go comments)\\n\\n---\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election through the **Raft consensus algorithm**, embedded in the server itself. The implementation spans multiple files in `server/etcdserver/`:\\n\\n**Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **raftNode** (raft.go): Manages the Raft state machine and leader election:\\n   - `tick()` function advances Raft election timeout counter\\n   - Detects leader transitions via `rd.SoftState.Lead` changes\\n   - `updateLeadership()` callback triggered on leader changes\\n   - Processes Raft protocol messages (RequestVote for elections, AppendEntries for heartbeats)\\n\\n2. **Election Mechanics** (raft.go, server/embed/config.go):\\n   - **Election Parameters** in embed/config.go:\\n     - `ElectionTicks`: Configurable election timeout in ticks (default 10)\\n     - `TickMs`: Heartbeat interval (default 100ms)\\n     - `InitialElectionTickAdvance`: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to accelerate initial election\\n     - `PreVote`: Raft pre-vote feature to reduce disruptive elections\\n   - **Election Flow**:\\n     - Followers start election when no heartbeat received within `ElectionTimeout` (ElectionTicks \u00d7 TickMs)\\n     - Send RequestVote RPC to all peers\\n     - Candidate becomes leader when receiving majority of votes\\n     - Leader periodically sends AppendEntries heartbeats\\n\\n3. **EtcdServer** (server.go): High-level server managing Raft state:\\n   - `Leader()` returns the current Raft leader ID\\n   - `waitLeader()` blocks until a leader is elected (waits for `raftStatusC` channel)\\n   - Monitors Raft state in the apply loop\\n   - Handles leader-specific operations (e.g., lease renewal, configuration changes)\\n\\n4. **Raft Message Transport** (api/rafthttp/transport.go):\\n   - `Transport` interface manages peer-to-peer Raft communication\\n   - Optimized stream for leader to send AppendEntries (heartbeats)\\n   - Leader detection via optimized message stream (only leader uses it)\\n\\n5. **Server Statistics** (api/v2stats/server.go):\\n   - `becomeLeader()` tracks leader state transitions\\n   - Metrics include leader ID, start time, and state (Leader/Follower/Candidate)\\n   - `LeaderInfo` structure exposes current leader for external monitoring\\n\\n6. **Client-Side Election API** (api/v3election/, client/v3/concurrency/election.go):\\n   - Independent election service leveraging leases and watches\\n   - `Campaign()`: Client waits to become leader\\n   - `Resign()`: Client voluntarily steps down\\n   - Allows application-level elections without modifying Raft itself\\n\\n**Failover & Re-election Mechanism:**\\n- **Automatic detection**: Followers detect leader failure when heartbeat misses exceed `ElectionTimeout`\\n- **Disruptive election prevention**:\\n  - Raft pre-vote prevents split votes during network partitions\\n  - `InitialElectionTickAdvance` reduces unnecessary elections on startup\\n  - Election timeout randomization (implicit in Raft protocol)\\n- **Lease handling across elections** (server.go, lease/lessor.go):\\n  - Old leader drops lease operations when it loses quorum\\n  - New leader extends TTL for remaining leases (adds `ElectionTimeout` buffer)\\n  - Checkpoint mechanism persists remaining TTL to prevent loss\\n- **Quorum requirement**: Leadership requires majority of cluster (prevents split-brain)\\n- **Term-based fencing**: Each term has monotonically increasing ID preventing old leaders from committing proposals\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Distributed lease (API-backed) | Raft consensus (embedded) |\\n| **Coordination** | Kubernetes API atomic updates | Raft quorum + term number |\\n| **Heartbeat** | Implicit (RenewTime timestamp) | Explicit AppendEntries messages |\\n| **Failover Time** | RenewDeadline (10s default) | ElectionTimeout (1s default) |\\n| **Quorum** | None (arbitrary backend) | Requires majority |\\n| **Clock Dependency** | High (skew tolerance configurable) | Low (ticks instead of wall-clock) |\\n| **Fencing** | Distributed consensus via API | Raft term numbers |\\n| **Leader Election Type** | Time-based (lease expiration) | Vote-based (quorum consensus) |\\n\\nBoth systems provide high availability guarantees but through different architectural approaches: Kubernetes leverages its control plane API for lightweight leader election, while etcd embeds consensus at the protocol level for stronger guarantees and faster failover.\"\n}\n",

`becomeLeader()` tracks leader state transitions\\n   - Metrics include leader ID, start time, and state (Leader/Follower/Candidate)\\n   - `LeaderInfo` structure exposes current leader for external monitoring\\n\\n6. **Client-Side Election API** (api/v3election/, client/v3/concurrency/election.go):\\n   - Independent election service leveraging leases and watches\\n   - `Campaign()`: Client waits to become leader\\n   - `Resign()`: Client voluntarily steps down\\n   - Allows application-level elections without modifying Raft itself\\n\\n**Failover & Re-election Mechanism:**\\n- **Automatic detection**: Followers detect leader failure when heartbeat misses exceed `ElectionTimeout`\\n- **Disruptive election prevention**:\\n  - Raft pre-vote prevents split votes during network partitions\\n  - `InitialElectionTickAdvance` reduces unnecessary elections on startup\\n  - Election timeout randomization (implicit in Raft protocol)\\n- **Lease handling across elections** (server.go, lease/lessor.go):\\n  - Old leader drops lease operations when it loses quorum\\n  - New leader extends TTL for remaining leases (adds `ElectionTimeout` buffer)\\n  - Checkpoint mechanism persists remaining TTL to prevent loss\\n- **Quorum requirement**: Leadership requires majority of cluster (prevents split-brain)\\n- **Term-based fencing**: Each term has monotonically increasing ID preventing old leaders from committing proposals\\n\\n---\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Distributed lease (API-backed) | Raft consensus (embedded) |\\n| **Coordination** | Kubernetes API atomic updates | Raft quorum + term number |\\n| **Heartbeat** | Implicit (RenewTime timestamp) | Explicit AppendEntries messages |\\n| **Failover Time** | RenewDeadline (10s default) | ElectionTimeout (1s default) |\\n| **Quorum** | None (arbitrary backend) | Requires majority |\\n| **Clock Dependency** | High (skew tolerance configurable) | Low (ticks instead of wall-clock) |\\n| **Fencing** | Distributed consensus via API | Raft term numbers |\\n| **Leader Election Type** | Time-based (lease expiration) | Vote-based (quorum consensus) |\\n\\nBoth systems provide high availability guarantees but through different architectural approaches: Kubernetes leverages its control plane API for lightweight leader election, while etcd embeds consensus at the protocol level for stronger guarantees and faster failover.\"\n}\n",
